  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

  <span id="freeText3227494676515169628" style="display:none"><i>Librarian's Note: Alternate cover for this ISBN can be found <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30556465" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</i><br /><br /><i>Four young ladies enter London society with one necessary goal: they must use their feminine wit and wiles to find a husband. So they band together, and a daring husband-hunting scheme is born.</i><br /><br /><b>It happened at the ball...</b><br /><br />Where beautiful but bold Lillian Bowman quickly learned that her independent American ways weren't entirely "the thing." And the most disapproving of all was insufferable, snobbish, and impossible Marcus, Lord Westcliff, London's most eligible aristocrat.<br /><br /><b>It happened in the garden...</b><br /><br />When Marcus shockingly—and dangerously—swept her into his arms. Lillian was overcome with a consuming passion for a man she didn't even like. Time stood still; it was as if no one else existed... thank goodness they weren't caught very nearly in the act!<br /><br /><b>It happened one autumn...</b><br /><br />Marcus was a man in charge of his own emotions, a bedrock of stability. But with Lillian, every touch was exquisite torture, every kiss an enticement for more. Yet how could he consider taking a woman so blatantly unsuitable... as his bride?</span>
  <a data-text-id="3227494676515169628" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_693050').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_693050').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});

          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“It has all the makings of a farce. One can scarcely conceive of a more ill-suited pair.”</b>
    </i>

</a><br><u>Books in Wallflowers series are stand-alones, but most enjoyed if read in order:</u><br><b>Book 0.5: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2265636218" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Again the Magic</a><br>Book 1: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/485389518" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Secrets of a Summer Night</a><br>Book 2: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/485389586" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">It Happened One Autumn</a><br>Book 3: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/485389576" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Devil in Winter</a><br>Book 4: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/485389666" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Scandal in Spring</a><br>Book 4.5: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/485389779" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">A Wallflower Christmas</a></b><br><br><b>It Happened One Autumn</b> (stand-alone) follows the unlikely romance between Lord, heir and investor <b>Marcus Marsden, The Eighth Earl of Westcliff</b> and American heiress and “wallflower” <b>Lillian Bowman, Lilly.</b><br><br>It’s lust-hate at first sight with the outspoken Lillian spending the Season in London to <b>catch a respectable, preferably titled husband.</b> She cannot stand to be around the stuffy Earl, though he makes her tingle in odd places.<br><br>Marcus <b>steers clear of the willful American</b> pretty much ever since he caught her playing baseball in her knickers. She might do things to his libido, but that does not make her wife material.<br><br>Follow their <b>tempestuous relationship</b> as they bicker, fight, challenge, argue, hate, steal kisses and lust after each other during an autumn party at Marcus’ country estate, year 1843. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517385048ra/24971842.gif" width="420" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Seven words to describe <b>Marcus Marsden, The Earl of Westcliff:</b> Trailblazer, charismatic, proper, loyal, hard-headed, graceful and noble.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517384778ra/24971838.gif" width="420" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Seven words to describe <b>Lillian Bowman, Lilly:</b> Opinionated, snarky, strong, stubborn, innocent, independent and loyal.<br><br><b>It Happened One Autumn,</b> told from dual POVs, is an <b>opposite attracts hate-to-love</b> romance with sexual tension overload, hilarious situations and bantering plus lots of obstacles along the way. Stellar character development in both the superb cast (to be featured in many more books) and the unforgettable Lord Westcliff and his Lillian.<br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“She could never fit into the mold of a Marsden wife.”<br>“Then the mold will have to be broken.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>

  <span id="freeText12038750692045628852" style="display:none"><b>4 Hate/Love Stars</b><br><br><b>******Spoilers*****</b><br><br><a href="http://s327.photobucket.com/user/jessica_hatfield1/media/13408498_zps3v3vi3jd.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484547850ra/21728029.gif" alt=" photo 13408498_zps3v3vi3jd.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>It Happened One Autumn was a good read but I didn't like it as much as I thought I would. I was really looking forward to Lillian's book. I loved her brash, foul mouthed, outspoken american ways. I couldn't wait for her to bring Westcliff to his knees. So I was a little disappointed that for half the book Westcliff fought his attraction to Lillian. I also didn't like that Lord St. Vincent was trying to court her or that they kissed. I wanted Westcliff to go after her like Simon from book one went after his wife! I did like Westcliff and loved Lillian. I enjoyed their relationship when they got around to having one. I even liked St. Vincent even though he acted like a villain towards the end. I am still looking forward to his book with Evie. Overall it was an enjoyable read! Just not as good as I expected.<br></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21987134" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14383255160339155413">Why are the best books the hardest to review? I'm not sure I can come up with enough superlatives for this one, the second book in Lisa Kleypas's magical <b>Wallflowers</b> series. I think she hit the ball out of the park with this humorous, emotional, romantic read!<br/><br/>I had my doubts coming into this, after reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/114162.Secrets_of_a_Summer_Night__Wallflowers___1_' title='Secrets of a Summer Night (Wallflowers, #1) by Lisa Kleypas' rel='nofollow noopener'>Secrets of a Summer Night</a>. In that book Marcus, Lord Westcliff (most eligible bachelor in England), was such an uptight, humorless stick-in-the-mud--how was I going to fall for him in his own </span>
  <span id="freeText14383255160339155413" style="display:none">Why are the best books the hardest to review? I'm not sure I can come up with enough superlatives for this one, the second book in Lisa Kleypas's magical <b>Wallflowers</b> series. I think she hit the ball out of the park with this humorous, emotional, romantic read!<br><br>I had my doubts coming into this, after reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/114162.Secrets_of_a_Summer_Night__Wallflowers___1_" title="Secrets of a Summer Night (Wallflowers, #1) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Secrets of a Summer Night</a>. In that book Marcus, Lord Westcliff (most eligible bachelor in England), was such an uptight, humorless stick-in-the-mud--how was I going to fall for him in his own book? Ahh, but LK did a 180 with his character, giving us his whole backstory (including brutal childhood), and I got to understand him, and fall in love with him right along with the heroine, American soap heiress Lillian Bowman.<br><br>Now, Lillian--I loved this girl despite (or maybe because) she was so opinionated, headstrong, irreverent, stubborn, sharp-tongued, funny,--and she took no guff from the button-downed, often arrogant Westcliff. Oh how they battled! Their arguing and sniping masked a heap of sexual tension between the two. He wanted her but hated that he did; she wanted him but hated that <i>she</i> did! You knew something had to give--who would be the first to break down and do something about it?<br><br>There were many, many scenes in this book that either made me laugh or made me sigh in satisfaction. Laughing? Any of the many conversations between Lillian and the other Wallflowers (Annabelle, Evie, Daisy--they had such fun together), but especially between Lillian and younger sister Daisy and the experiments with the perfume that Lillian insisted worked as an aphrodesiac. I also got a chuckle out of Westcliff and his friends (Hunt, St. Vincent, Shaw) discussing the frequency of their sexual liasons, and the time Hunt caught Westcliff and Lillian in a compromising position and teased him about his "once a week" beliefs.<br><br>The sighing? When Westcliff decides to give Lillian a few pointers about how to bat; their first kiss while hiding behind the hedgerow; the scene in the Butterfly Court (smokin' hot); the scene with the pear brandy (funny <i>and</i> scorching hot); when Westcliff professes his feelings and tells Lillian that she can be whoever she wants to be as long as she's with him; the poached pear scene (yowza!); and finally, when Westcliff stands up to his viper of a mother and tells her where to go! Yay, Marcus!<br><br>As usual, Kleypas's story is superbly written, with vivid descriptions of the characters, the food (the calf's head!), the clothing, and Westfield's beautiful estate of Stony Cross Park. Kleypas leaves no stone unturned in her storytelling--the characters backstories and every emotion are all layed out for the reader to enjoy--I felt that I was right there in the 1840s English countryside, witnessing it all.<br><br>Now LK threw a bit of a curveball that I didn't see coming, regarding St. Vincent (who I was liking just fine), that made me dislike him. Now how is she going to redeem him in his book (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/114166.Devil_in_Winter__Wallflowers___3_" title="Devil in Winter (Wallflowers, #3) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Devil in Winter</a>)? I can't wait to find out! I don't know if she can top this one, which earns 5 big stars!<br><br>Westcliff (as I see him)...<br><a href="http://s880.photobucket.com/albums/ac3/aunteecr/?action=view&amp;current=westcliff.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380311060i/688363._SY540_.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14383255160339155413" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1339129662" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1339129662" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1339129662?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=regency">regency</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1339129662" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1881447176533704634">There are guilty pleasures, and there are Guilty Pleasures. <br/><b><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/827412.It_Happened_One_Autumn?ac=1&from_search=true' rel='nofollow noopener'>It Happened One Autumn</a> is a Guilty Pleasure.</b> <br/><br/><i>Four young ladies enter London society with one necessary goal: they must use their feminine wit and wiles to find a husband. So they band together, and a daring husband-hunting scheme is born.</i><br/><br/>It Happened One Autumn follows the second Wallflower, the bold and shockingly opinionated <b>Lillian Bowman</b>, whose crude manners, American origins and nouveau riche status complicate her attempts to find a</span>
  <span id="freeText1881447176533704634" style="display:none">There are guilty pleasures, and there are Guilty Pleasures. <br><b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/827412.It_Happened_One_Autumn?ac=1&amp;from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">It Happened One Autumn</a> is a Guilty Pleasure.</b> <br><br><i>Four young ladies enter London society with one necessary goal: they must use their feminine wit and wiles to find a husband. So they band together, and a daring husband-hunting scheme is born.</i><br><br>It Happened One Autumn follows the second Wallflower, the bold and shockingly opinionated <b>Lillian Bowman</b>, whose crude manners, American origins and nouveau riche status complicate her attempts to find a noble husband in English society. Her improper comments and attitude are met with contempt, but no one is more annoyed at her stubborness and inability to act like a delicate young woman than <b>Lord Westcliff</b>, an overbearing and controlling nobleman who happens to be the most eligible bachelor. Their fights are legendary, their pigheadedness equal. But aside from their mutual annoyance, there is something else brewing; something that shimmers and burns, passion and attraction and a deeper connection that entangle them in a web of stolen kisses, unyielding egotism and a love that may endanger Marcus' heritage and everything he's struggled to achieve. The question is, <i>what will he choose? His legacy, or the only woman that challenges him and makes him feel alive?</i><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Oh, Daisy, it's revolting the way I want to fawn all over him. I'm afraid I'm going to do something dreadfully silly today. Burst into song or something. For God's sake, don't let me.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>It Happened One Autumn is not a literary masterpiece. It's not a work of art that inspires poems and frenzied reviews glorifying the prose or the concept; you won't find deep meanings conveyed in its pages. It will not rattle you to the core, or make you a better person after you finish it. However, I don't give a single darn. Because in all honesty, I <b>devoured</b> it in less than 24 hours and <b>I had the time of my life</b>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1540828963ra/26516761.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>It was delicious, sensual, funny, with a dash of suspense and a flock of butterflies upsetting my stomach.</b> Lisa Kleypas used autumn hues, and painted lavish balls, picturesque gardens, a rainbow of dresses and delicacies that transported me to another time, another society that was beautiful and cruel, that sucked me in its ways and expectations and left me dazed. Marcus and Lillian give the definition to <b>enemies-to-lovers</b>. He wanted to tame her; she wantet to prove him that she is a capable woman, proud of her choices, a woman who shall not be controlled. Their fights were like fireworks. But their <i>other</i> scenes, well,<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467676229ra/19616875.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Their chemistry was insane</b>. They collided with the force of two meteorites, but they also connected in an emotional level that made me all warm and fuzzy. And even though I found Lillian's behavior <b>over the top</b> (hello <b>3.5 stars</b>), fighting for the sake of fighting, throwing tantrums and opposing to common sense for no reason at all, their relationship <b> utterly endearing</b>. <br>And (surprise!) I fell in love with Marcus, with his uptight and his protective and his <b>wicked</b> side.<br><br>*gulp*<br><br>So, <b> if you're up for a fun ride, and a blazing historical romance, do try the Wallflowers!</b><br><br>P.S. I don't know if the next book will be my cup of tea. After the things St. Vincent did in this one, I find it hard to impossible to even like him, let alone consider him a love interest.<br><br><a href="http://booknest.eu/reviews/kat/1369-ithappenedoneautumn" rel="nofollow noopener">You can find this review and more on BookNest!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1881447176533704634" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6561363-it-happened-one-autumn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=paperback">paperback</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2168042309" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12004316649263011211"><b> 4.5 stars! </b><br/><br/><b> <i> “The next time you face a room full of strangers . . . you might tell yourself that some of them are just friends waiting to be found.” </i> </b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509597224ra/24339979.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The Wallflowers are so good!!! I think this book is my favorite in the series so far (yes, I have read Devil in Winter already). I liked the chemistry between the main characters in this one the most so far, that hate to love you tension. This book is the story of Lillian and Westcliff, a brash and outspoken American and a formal, follow the rules</span>
  <span id="freeText12004316649263011211" style="display:none"><b> 4.5 stars! </b><br><br><b> <i> “The next time you face a room full of strangers . . . you might tell yourself that some of them are just friends waiting to be found.” </i> </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509597224ra/24339979.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The Wallflowers are so good!!! I think this book is my favorite in the series so far (yes, I have read Devil in Winter already). I liked the chemistry between the main characters in this one the most so far, that hate to love you tension. This book is the story of Lillian and Westcliff, a brash and outspoken American and a formal, follow the rules Englishmen. Right off the bat they cannot stand each other, but as time goes by they realize their hatred for each other might be something more.<br><br><b> <i> “I can't get it out," she said.<br>"Just pull at it."<br>"It hurts. It's throbbing."<br>"Pull harder."<br>"I can't! It's truly stuck. I need something to make it slippery. Do you have some sort of lubricant nearby?"<br>"No."<br>"Not anything?"<br>"Much as it may surprise you, we've never needed lubricant in the library before now.” </i> </b><br><br>I'm not normally one for historical romance, but Lisa Kleypas has that magic about her writing. It's never cheesy to me (and I loathe cheesy historical), and never do I roll my eyes at the language or the diction. It's an amazing escape from reality, a foray into the lives and loves of the past.<br><br>I'm also going to add, when Lillian and Westcliff do finally give in, BOOM WENT THE OVARIES! You wanna read it now, don't you?<br><br><b> <i> “There is nothing on earth more beautiful to me than your smile...no sound sweeter than your laughter...no pleasure greater than holding you in my arms." </i> </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1494101706i/22685352._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Follow me on ♥ <a href="http://www.facebook.com/rachelreadsravenously" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> ♥ <a href="http://rachelsreadsravenously.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> ♥ <a href="http://instagram.com/rachelreadsravenously" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ♥ <a href="https://twitter.com/rayliz89" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ♥</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Amy | Foxy Blogs by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister">Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9955253-amy-foxy-blogs?shelf=donum">donum</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9955253-amy-foxy-blogs?shelf=2015-books">2015-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9955253-amy-foxy-blogs?shelf=headphones">headphones</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9955253-amy-foxy-blogs?shelf=july-2015">july-2015</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer757178761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6497030291298965858"><b>FOUR POINT FIVE STARS</b><br/><br/><b>THE HUSBAND HUNTERS ARE BACK!</b><br/>In London (1843) a pact is made between 4 wallflowers. They will help each other find husbands starting with the oldest and working down to the youngest. <br/><br/>(1) Annabelle is the oldest of the pact. <i>Married - first book.</i><br/>(2) <b>Lillian</b> is a rich American who has not acclimated to England.<br/>(3) Evie is painfully shy and stutters.<br/>(4) Daisy is the younger sister to Lillian. <br/><br/><b>IT HAPPENED ONE AUTUMN</b> is another GREAT installment in this series of wallflowers. <b>Lil</b></span>
  <span id="freeText6497030291298965858" style="display:none"><b>FOUR POINT FIVE STARS</b><br><br><b>THE HUSBAND HUNTERS ARE BACK!</b><br>In London (1843) a pact is made between 4 wallflowers. They will help each other find husbands starting with the oldest and working down to the youngest. <br><br>(1) Annabelle is the oldest of the pact. <i>Married - first book.</i><br>(2) <b>Lillian</b> is a rich American who has not acclimated to England.<br>(3) Evie is painfully shy and stutters.<br>(4) Daisy is the younger sister to Lillian. <br><br><b>IT HAPPENED ONE AUTUMN</b> is another GREAT installment in this series of wallflowers. <b>Lillian</b> is the next one in line to find a husband. She's unlike anything the English men are use to. She's a rich American who comes off a little more wild and free than her English counterparts.<br><br>Then we have FOREVER and lifetime bachelor,<b> Marcus, Lord Westcliff</b>. His attraction to the brazen American girl is hidden from everyone. Being mixed up with someone of her standard wouldn't look good for his family lineage. <br><br>In comes the play of a special perfume that holds a secret ingredient that turns men hot and heavy for you. Any time Marcus gets within a close distance to Lillian his animal magnetism goes wild for her.<br><br>Towards the end of the book there's a little plot twist that I didn't see coming which made for a fun adventure. <br><br>I read part of this and listened to the audio for the other half. If you haven't read a Lisa Kleypas book you should give them a try. They're well written with interesting plot lines. <br><br><b>SERIES:</b><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/114162.Secrets_of_a_Summer_Night__Wallflowers___1_" title="Secrets of a Summer Night (Wallflowers, #1) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1298443922s/114162.jpg" alt="Secrets of a Summer Night (Wallflowers, #1) by Lisa Kleypas" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/827412.It_Happened_One_Autumn__Wallflowers___2_" title="It Happened One Autumn (Wallflowers, #2) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1388206425s/827412.jpg" alt="It Happened One Autumn (Wallflowers, #2) by Lisa Kleypas" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer49907547" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16320942441146106195"><i>Re-read 10/11/19</i>:<br/><br/>Just as wonderful as I remember from almost 10 years ago!! Still big 5++ stars!!<br/><br/><i>Original read/review Jan'2010</i>:<br/><br/>5++ stars – Historical Romance<br/><br/>WOW! I <i>loooved</i> this second installment in Kleypas’s extraordinary <i>Wallflowers</i> series about four very different young ladies in Victorian era England society whose deep bond of friendship sustains them through the trials and tribulations of life, family, relationships, and love. <br/> <br/>Wealthy American heiress Lillian Bowman is fiercely independent</span>
  <span id="freeText16320942441146106195" style="display:none"><i>Re-read 10/11/19</i>:<br /><br />Just as wonderful as I remember from almost 10 years ago!! Still big 5++ stars!!<br /><br /><i>Original read/review Jan'2010</i>:<br /><br />5++ stars – Historical Romance<br /><br />WOW! I <i>loooved</i> this second installment in Kleypas’s extraordinary <i>Wallflowers</i> series about four very different young ladies in Victorian era England society whose deep bond of friendship sustains them through the trials and tribulations of life, family, relationships, and love. <br /> <br />Wealthy American heiress Lillian Bowman is fiercely independent, strong-willed, feisty, daring, obstinate, brash, honest, outspoken, free-spirited, opinionated...pretty much everything lacking and undesirable in a proper English bride befitting of someone as renowned as London’s most sought after bachelor, Marcus, Lord Westcliff. That’s just fine by Lillian, because the last thing she wants is a domineering, stuffy, snobby, dogmatic, pompous aristocrat for a husband. But it doesn’t take long before sparks fly and fireworks explode between the two stubborn rivals who have a lot more in common than either of them wants to admit, and their intense attraction and volatile passion soon becomes too strong to ignore. <br /><br />Boy oh boy did I love these two willful hardheads together! Talk about powerful, electric zing-chemistry...Marcus and Lillian had it in spades! I enjoyed their sarcastic, witty banter and spirited arguments, and their smoldering hot passion scorched the pages. But most of all, I loved the tender, romantic moments (like the scene below) that demonstrated how perfect Marcus and Lillian are together.<br /><br />Marcus, Lord Westcliff:<br /><br /><i>“Rest. You’ll need to regain your strength...because once we’re married, I won’t be able to leave you alone. I’ll want to love you every hour, every minute of the day.” He nestled her more closely against him. “There is nothing on earth more beautiful to me than your smile...no sound sweeter than your laughter...no pleasure greater than holding you in my arms. I realized today that I could never live without you, stubborn little hellion that you are. In this life and the next, you’re my only hope of happiness. Tell me, Lillian, dearest love...how can you have reached so far inside my heart?” He paused to kiss her damp silken skin...and smiled as the wisp of a feminine snore broke the peaceful silence.</i><br /><br /><b>It Happened One Autumn</b> is a remarkable, intensely romantic, and enchanting read that will hold a top place on my keeper shelf for years to come! <i>Verrry big</i> 5 stars! <br /><br />And just for fun and laughs, I had to capture the hilarious scene between the wallflower gals discussing, or perhaps more accurately, vehemently dismissing, Evie’s rather portly cousin Eustace being her one and only marital prospect.<br /><br /><i>“Wait a minute,” Daisy said suspiciously, coming to Lillian’s side. <br />“We’ve met Evie’s cousin Eustace before. Lillian, do you remember the ball at Winterbourne House?” Her eyes narrowed accusingly. “He was the one who broke the chair, wasn’t he, Evie?”<br />Evie confirmed Daisy’s question with an inarticulate murmur.<br />“Good God!” Lillian exclaimed, “you are not considering marrying him, Evie!”<br />Annabelle wore a puzzled expression. “How did he break the chair? Does he have a foul temper? Did he throw it?”<br />“He broke it by sitting on it,” Lillian said with a scowl.<br />“Cousin Eustace is rather l-large boned,” Evie admitted. <br />“Cousin Eustace has more chins than I’ve got fingers,” Lillian said impatiently. “And he was so busy filling his face during the ball that he couldn’t be bothered to make conversation.”<br />“When I went to shake his hand,” Daisy added, “I came away with a half-eaten wing of roast chicken.”<br />“He forgot that he was holding it,” Evie said apologetically. “He did say he was sorry for ruining your glove, as I recall.”<br />Daisy frowned. “That didn’t bother me nearly as much as the question of where he was hiding the rest of the chicken.”</i><br /><br />BUWAHAhaHAhahaha!!!! That scene just flat-out cracked me up! :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="16320942441146106195" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/83869023?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" href="/user/show/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish">UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish</a>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=author-lisa-kleypas">author-lisa-kleypas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=2010-reads">2010-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=reviewed-by-me">reviewed-by-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=own-have-read">own-have-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=series-wallflowers-kleypas">series-wallflowers-kleypas</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer83869023" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4152822830731636502"><br/>Wow! Another fun installment of The Wallflowers series.<br/><br/>I love the way Lisa Kleypas developes her characters. Subtly, without pages and pages of narrative descriptives. We learn about them by seeing them in action, or through the eyes of others.<br/><br/>It was such a joy to watch Marcus, Lord Westcliff, put aside the bitterness of his childhood, the will of his mother and the demands of his title and just allow himself to experience the emotions which, despite his best efforts, were awakened by Lillian Bo</span>
  <span id="freeText4152822830731636502" style="display:none"><br />Wow! Another fun installment of The Wallflowers series.<br /><br />I love the way Lisa Kleypas developes her characters. Subtly, without pages and pages of narrative descriptives. We learn about them by seeing them in action, or through the eyes of others.<br /><br />It was such a joy to watch Marcus, Lord Westcliff, put aside the bitterness of his childhood, the will of his mother and the demands of his title and just allow himself to experience the emotions which, despite his best efforts, were awakened by Lillian Bowman.<br /><br />And it was also a joy to watch Lillian put aside her own preconceived notions of Marcus, the man, and allow herself to accept her feelings of love for him, and accept his love for her as well.<br /><br />Marcus and Lillian are fabulous together. When they get together they bring out the worst in each other, but they also bring out the best in one another.<br /><br />OK, I just want to say that there are 2 scenes that stand out in my mind and both made me laugh. I won't go into detail so as not to ruin it for anyone who hasn't read this... but who didn't laugh at baked calf's head and dingy dipper butterflies? Don't deny it, if you've read this book, you laughed. And the other scene was where Annabelle, having come down to breakfast with dark circles under her eyes and looking as though she hadn't slept at all during the night (because she hadn't) was trying to delicately explain to Lillian, Evie and Daisy the effect that a certain perfume had had on Simon, her husband, who needed no potion to influence or increase his sexual... virility.<br /><br />And it would be shameful if I didn't mention that there are some very steamy sexual encounters that were... how can I put this... <i>steamy</i>. I may never look at pears the same way again. *sigh*<br /><br />Well, needless to say, while I enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/114162.Secrets_of_a_Summer_Night__Wallflowers___1_" title="Secrets of a Summer Night (Wallflowers, #1) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Secrets of a Summer Night</a> , <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/827412.It_Happened_One_Autumn__Wallflowers___2_" title="It Happened One Autumn (Wallflowers, #2) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">It Happened One Autumn</a> has made me a Lisa Kleypas fan!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4152822830731636502" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2317872472" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2317872472" />
    <a title="Phrynne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8655084-phrynne"><img alt="Phrynne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577753809p2/8655084.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2317872472?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2018</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer17478037586728262500">Another entertaining entry in the Wallflower series, all of which have been thoroughly enjoyable even if I did read them out of order!<br/><br/>This time it is Lillian's turn to find herself a rich husband and she does it in style. As in all the other books the dialogue is the thing- smart and funny and always entertaining. The characters are well defined and as I am sure I have said before, probably many times, the overall atmosphere of the book is a la <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/18067.Georgette_Heyer' title='Georgette Heyer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Georgette Heyer</a> but with sex. And this is not a bad</span>
  <span id="freeText17478037586728262500" style="display:none">Another entertaining entry in the Wallflower series, all of which have been thoroughly enjoyable even if I did read them out of order!<br /><br />This time it is Lillian's turn to find herself a rich husband and she does it in style. As in all the other books the dialogue is the thing- smart and funny and always entertaining. The characters are well defined and as I am sure I have said before, probably many times, the overall atmosphere of the book is a la <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/18067.Georgette_Heyer" title="Georgette Heyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Georgette Heyer</a> but with sex. And this is not a bad thing.<br /><br />Sad that this series is finished but luckily <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/27847.Lisa_Kleypas" title="Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Lisa Kleypas</a> has written others! <br /><br /></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elise ✘ a.k.a Ryder&#39;s Pet ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elise ✘ a.k.a Ryder&#39;s Pet ✘" href="/user/show/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet">Elise ✘ a.k.a Ryder&#39;s Pet ✘</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6561363-it-happened-one-autumn">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Elise ✘ a.k.a Ryder's Pet ✘ by: </span>

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1660643239" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer297268283354982880"><blockquote>
  <b>⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱*No Longer For Me*⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱</b>
</blockquote> <br/><b><u>Re-read</u>:</b><br/>The book centers around American heiress <b>Lillian Odelle Bowman</b> (24?) and <b>Marcus Marsden</b> (35), Lord Westcliff, the Earl of Westcliff. Lillian is looking for a husband in England, what she didn't expect was finding the arrogant Lord Marcus interesting.... I don't know how, but somehow I obviously liked Lillian the first time reading it, this time however? I almost hated her at some point. Her recklessness and actions when people say no to her are insane. </span>
  <span id="freeText297268283354982880" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱*No Longer For Me*⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱</b>
</blockquote> <br><b><u>Re-read</u>:</b><br>The book centers around American heiress <b>Lillian Odelle Bowman</b> (24?) and <b>Marcus Marsden</b> (35), Lord Westcliff, the Earl of Westcliff. Lillian is looking for a husband in England, what she didn't expect was finding the arrogant Lord Marcus interesting.... I don't know how, but somehow I obviously liked Lillian the first time reading it, this time however? I almost hated her at some point. Her recklessness and actions when people say no to her are insane. She feels the need to prove herself someway and actually put others in danger in doing so. She almost hurt a horse to prove a point that she could do something, when it was obvious that she couldn't. Marcus thinks Lillian an ill-natured brat, and I actually tend to agree. She has too much pride in herself, and it's annoying. She's also, in my eyes, a bit selfish. <i>‘‘Your Grace, she thought. That was what Westcliff would have to call her, once St. Vincent came into his title. First she would be Lady St. Vincent, and then the Duchess of Kingston. She would be above Westcliff socially, and she would never let him forget it. Your Grace, she repeated, comforting herself with the syllables. Your Grace…’’</i><br><br>It's pathetic. She's quite pathetic, to be honest. Her character ruined the whole book for me. I couldn't stand her. The moments between Marcus and Lillian were the only thing that was interesting and worth reading. The last 30% or so I started to skim a lot. I considered quitting it, but when I had come so far, I might as well finish it. That being said, the female character ruined the whole book, made me roll my eyes at her <i>many</i> times, but Marcus was interesting and hot. Marcus was the only thing in the book that was readable, the rest was meh and the female was annoying. Strange how I didn't notice the first time reading it.... I seem to have liked it a lot the first time around :O <br><br><b><u>Other Characters</u>:</b><br><i>The list is a bit long so I've put it in a spoilers tag.</i><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[→ <b>Daisy Bowman</b>, Lillian's little sister. The girls’ father, <b>Thomas Bowman</b> owned a New York business enterprise that manufactured scents and soaps. Mrs. <b>Mercedes Bowman</b>, their mother.<br>→ Mr. <b>Phineas Nettle</b>, owner of a perfumery.<br>→ Lady <b>Olivia ‘Livia’ Shaw</b>, Marcus' little sister. Just wedded to <b>Gideon Shaw</b>, of the New York Shaws. Gideon was Marcus' friend and was that most contradictory of terms, an “American aristocrat,” the great-grandson of an ambitious Yankee sea captain.<br>→ Lady <b>Aline</b>, Marcus' little sister. She lived with her husband, <b>McKenna</b> in New York.<br>→ <b>Annabelle <s>Peyton</s> Hunt</b>, Lillian's friend and member of the wallflowers, the self-named group of girls who had met while sitting at the side of every ball and soiree last season. They had all sworn to help one another find husbands. Their efforts had resulted in Annabelle’s successful match with Mr. <b>Simon Hunt</b> just two months ago. Annabelle married Westcliff’s best friend, was as an entrepreneur, a former butcher’s son who was shrewd, enterprising, and trustworthy in every regard. <br>→ <b>Evangeline ‘Evie’ Jenner</b>, Lillian's friend and member of the wallflowers. Her aunt, <b>Florence</b>. Cousin <b>Eustace</b>, Florence's son, who she want Evie to marry.<br>→ <b>Arthur</b>, a stableboy working for Marcus.<br>→ Lord <b> Sebastian St. Vincent</b>, a viscount and friend of Marcus. He's an unprincipled scoundrel and a prolific lover of women.<br>→ Lady <b>Westcliff</b>/The Countess of Westcliff, Marcus’s mother.<br>→ <b>Raphael</b>, Lillian's oldest brother. <br>→ <b>Ransom</b> and <b>Rhys</b>, twins and brothers of Lillian. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You create trouble from thin air,” Mercedes said, her eyes slitted. “Which is why I am going to supervise the pair of you closely. After your behavior on our last visit here, I am amazed that we were invited back.”<br>“I’m not,” Lillian rejoined dryly. “Everyone knows that we’re here because Westcliff has an eye on Father’s company.”<br>“Lord Westcliff,” Mercedes corrected with a hiss. “Lillian, you must refer to him with respect! He is the wealthiest peer in England, with a bloodline—”<br>“—that’s older than the queen’s,” Daisy interrupted in a singsong tone, having heard this speech on a multitude of occasions. “And the oldest earldom in Britain, which makes him—”<br>“—the most eligible bachelor in Europe,” Lillian finished dryly, raising her brows with mock significance. “Maybe the entire world. Mother, if you’re actually hoping that Westcliff is going to marry either of us, you’re a lunatic.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b><u>Quick basic facts</u>:</b><br><b>Genre</b>: - (Adult) Historical Romance (M/F).<br><b>Series</b>: - Series (Can Be Read As A Standalone), Book Two.<br><b>Love triangle?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Not really. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>Cheating?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>HEA?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Yes. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>Favorite character?</b> - Marcus Marsden.<br><b>Would I read more by this author/or of series?</b> - Unsure.<br><b>Would I recommend this book/series?</b> - Not really.<br><b>Will I read this again in the future?</b> - Definitely not.<br><b>New Rating</b> - 2/1.5 stars.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445268775i/16623124.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b><u>First read</u>:</b><br>I actually liked it. Really liked it.<br><b>Rate: 3.5/4 stars</b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/797536731?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina ~ Brunette Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina ~ Brunette Reader" href="/user/show/19958389-christina-brunette-reader">Christina ~ Brunette Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19958389-christina-brunette-reader?shelf=victorian-early-1837-1850">victorian-early-1837-1850</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19958389-christina-brunette-reader?shelf=historical-romance-victorian">historical-romance-victorian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer797536731" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16133505478468975137"><br/><i>
  <b>3,5 Stars</b>
</i><br/><br/>One thing's for sure: Westcliff, the hero, has much more patience for ill-mannered houseguests than I do. The houseguest in question being the heroine, Miss Lillian Bowman. <br/><br/>The brash American heiress and the starchy English earl, so much potential especially in the hand of such a skilled author, and in fact, for the greater part the book delivered on all accounts and I enjoyed most of their scenes together immensely. If only Lillian had been a little less confrontational. I understa</span>
  <span id="freeText16133505478468975137" style="display:none"><br /><i>
  <b>3,5 Stars</b>
</i><br /><br />One thing's for sure: Westcliff, the hero, has much more patience for ill-mannered houseguests than I do. The houseguest in question being the heroine, Miss Lillian Bowman. <br /><br />The brash American heiress and the starchy English earl, so much potential especially in the hand of such a skilled author, and in fact, for the greater part the book delivered on all accounts and I enjoyed most of their scenes together immensely. If only Lillian had been a little less confrontational. I understand, and appreciate, <i>feisty</i>, but she bordered on rude several times and showed an animosity towards the hero that really had no solid ground, so the "opposites attracts" trope often felt overplayed to me.<br />The closed confines of Stony Cross, Westcliff's country estate, where the whole story takes place, didn't allow for much action or plot twists and all the (slightly over-the-top) drama was concentrated in the very last section, though the lively dialogues, the sparkly banters between the leads and their off the charts chemistry, the humour and the flowing writing more than made up for it. And Westcliff, now he was a dear and sexy one.<br />It also was nice to meet once again the Wallflowers and the other cast of characters and follow their further interactions which, as I've already found in book 1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/114162.Secrets_of_a_Summer_Night__Wallflowers___1_" title="Secrets of a Summer Night (Wallflowers, #1) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Secrets of a Summer Night</a>, were some of the best fun.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16133505478468975137" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer396587478" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17461271351567668311"><b>When love makes you lose control.</b><br/><br/>This is my favourite in the series. Nothing gets my heart pumping (in my reads) like a hero who listens to his heart instead of his head. When the hero is dumbfounded, discombobulated and bamboozled by his feelings, I can't help but want to sigh. I love that his mind is telling him that she's all wrong but his heart and body are saying *come a little bit closer*. They <i>try</i> to ignore <b>it</b>. They <i>try</i> to fight <b>it</b>. They run screaming from <b>it</b>. But <b>IT</b> is too much. Those bl</span>
  <span id="freeText17461271351567668311" style="display:none"><b>When love makes you lose control.</b><br /><br />This is my favourite in the series. Nothing gets my heart pumping (in my reads) like a hero who listens to his heart instead of his head. When the hero is dumbfounded, discombobulated and bamboozled by his feelings, I can't help but want to sigh. I love that his mind is telling him that she's all wrong but his heart and body are saying *come a little bit closer*. They <i>try</i> to ignore <b>it</b>. They <i>try</i> to fight <b>it</b>. They run screaming from <b>it</b>. But <b>IT</b> is too much. Those blasted feelings won't leave.<br /><br />Marcus fought a valiant battle but love...and Lillian, were the winners.<br /><br />One of the most unlikely couples to ever fall in love, in the end, they were a perfect match for each other. His stiff upper lip will remind Lillian to be a lady every so often. Her adventurous spirit will help Marcus to have fun once in awhile. I love it when opposites attract.<br /><br />This series is one of my all-time favourites in historical romance. <i>Lisa Kleypas</i> writes lovable characters and the <i>Wallflowers</i> are some of the best. If you haven't read this series and thinking of trying out historical romance, I definitely recommend.<br /><br />The audio was amazing and I think Rosalyn Landor is my go-to narrator for Historical Romance. Her voice is easy to listen to, the accents spot-on and she does very well with the male characters too. I never struggle with telling the characters apart.<br /><br />I will definitely be going on in the series and with that ending, I think it will be sooner rather than later.<br /><br />No change in my rating as I loved the audio as much as reading It Happened One Autumn.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17461271351567668311" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_36563943" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/36563943" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/36563943?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Victorian romance fans who enjoy a British/American pairing</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=opposites-attract">opposites-attract</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=favorite-or-autobuy-author">favorite-or-autobuy-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=owned-copy">owned-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=victorian">victorian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=british-american-paired">british-american-paired</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer36563943" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4925800194048689588">This was a great second entry into the Wallflower series. I really enjoyed this story and I firmly believe that Lillian and Westcliff are soulmates. They are both strong, vital people who are not afraid to say what they think and do what they want to do. Westcliff is a very arrogant man and very opinionated. He came off as being a little bit snobby in some ways. Not in the sense that he was too good to associate with self-made men of working class origins. He was very forward-thinking in that ma</span>
  <span id="freeText4925800194048689588" style="display:none">This was a great second entry into the Wallflower series. I really enjoyed this story and I firmly believe that Lillian and Westcliff are soulmates. They are both strong, vital people who are not afraid to say what they think and do what they want to do. Westcliff is a very arrogant man and very opinionated. He came off as being a little bit snobby in some ways. Not in the sense that he was too good to associate with self-made men of working class origins. He was very forward-thinking in that manner. But he was snobby in how he viewed Lillian and her sister, because they were brash Americans. Lillian is very forward thinking, and would never fit into the mold of a well-bred, quiet, English lady. Westcliff thinks that's exactly what he wants if he marries. But he's not in a hurry to marry anyway, although he knows he must. I think he was waiting for that spark that exploded when Lillian came into the picture. Perhaps his snooty attitude toward Lillian was just his way of keeping a barrier up against her. Westcliff fought his feelings for Lillian for as long as he could. But I have to give it to him, when he fell, he fell hard. <br><br>I enjoyed the way Lillian needled him. Westcliff had a tendency to take himself way too seriously. He needed to loosen up. Lillian starts out finding him too high in the instep and too stuffy and far too bossy, but at the same time, she's fiercely attracted to his muscular vitality and virlity. Westcliff is a keen sportsman and athlete. I like that he believes in working hard and isn't a rake (this was a nice change for a character who was very much of the aristocracy). I think this aura also won over Lillian. There is no question about the strong attraction between Lillian and Westcliff, and it drives this book towards its inevitable conclusion.<br><br>In this story, my favorite hero, St. Vincent, is more of a villain. What he does was very ill-advised, and he pays for it the hard way. Luckily it helps to show Marcus, Lord Westcliff, what he is about to allow to slip through his fingers. Maybe that's why Westcliff can't stay mad at him. <br><br>I can't say this is one of my favorites by LK. I think it's because Westcliff and Lillian are very abrasive characters who I love in small doses, but can overwhelm me in large doses. But, LK has never written a bad book and she never will, in my opinion. And this book fits so seemlessly into the Wallflower series (with crossover with Again the Magic since Marcus is Aline's older brother) that it's going to be a keeper by default. <br><br><br>Actors I would cast as Westcliff and Lillian: Jamie Bamber and Natalie Portman.<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br><br><span>[image error]</span><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="4925800194048689588" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2219667628" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9703544004396618904"><b>★4.5★</b><blockquote>
  <b>"I've wanted you every moment since I first held you in my arms."</b>
</blockquote><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519419931i/25111974.jpg' width='' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>It Happened One Autumn</b> is the second book in the Wallflowers Series. Relatively new to Historical Romance, I have discovered Lisa Kleypas to be one of my new favorite go-to authors. The Wallflowers features four young ladies living in London as they try to secure happiness and love. In this second book, we are introduced to the spunky American Lillian Bowman and the noble aristocrat Lord Marcus Westcliff. Lillian and her f</span>
  <span id="freeText9703544004396618904" style="display:none"><b>★4.5★</b><blockquote>
  <b>"I've wanted you every moment since I first held you in my arms."</b>
</blockquote><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519419931i/25111974.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>It Happened One Autumn</b> is the second book in the Wallflowers Series. Relatively new to Historical Romance, I have discovered Lisa Kleypas to be one of my new favorite go-to authors. The Wallflowers features four young ladies living in London as they try to secure happiness and love. In this second book, we are introduced to the spunky American Lillian Bowman and the noble aristocrat Lord Marcus Westcliff. Lillian and her family are guests at Lord Westcliff's Manor. Lillian and Marcus are complete opposites and yet, together they are a perfect match. Marcus is quite wealthy and wants for nothing and Lillian is an unpolished, outspoken, American Girl just trying to find acceptance in society. At first, Marcus finds Ms. Bowman to be a reckless savage and yet, as they spend more time together a fiery attraction develops between the two. Lillian is not an ideal candidate for a bride for Lord Westcliff but they manage to fall head over heels in love with each other. Can Marcus truly set aside his family obligations and overlook the rules of society in order to wed an unruly American woman?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466701540i/19510149._SX540_.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>
  <b>"There is nothing on earth more beautiful to me than your smile..."</b>
</blockquote> Told in dual POV, <b>It Happened One Autumn</b> offers a tender and passionate love story with plenty of laughs. Lillian and Marcus share a charged relationship full of tension and heated seduction. Throughout the verbal warfare these two characters experience, the connection becomes real and authentic. The supporting characters offer intrigue and humor as Marcus and Lillian discover the truth about their fate! I highly recommend this book to HR fans and cannot wait to meet more of the Wallflowers! Although I am sure it is best to read the series in order, each book can be read as a stand-alone. Lisa Kleypas is a gifted storyteller who will transport you to another world! <br><br><b>***Wallflowers***<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/674220.Again_the_Magic__Wallflowers___0_5_" title="Again the Magic (Wallflowers, #0.5) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1418771403s/674220.jpg" alt="Again the Magic (Wallflowers, #0.5) by <div id="review_332020100" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/332020100" />
    <a title="Karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6972914-karen"><img alt="Karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529600203p2/6972914.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/332020100?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen" href="/user/show/6972914-karen">Karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6972914-karen?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer332020100" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8120593139009592298"><b>5 STARS</b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1558279161i/27541031._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>Staring down at her adorably pursed lips, he felt an insistent warmth invading his heart, overflowing and spilling past its fretted barriers. God in heaven, he was tired of fighting his desire for her. It was exhausting to struggle against something so overwhelming. Like trying not to breathe.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/>I absolutely LOVED this one. Delightfully entertaining, and at times hilariously funny. This was an enemies to lovers connection that was incredibly addicting. There were several scenes t</span>
  <span id="freeText8120593139009592298" style="display:none"><b>5 STARS</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1558279161i/27541031._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>Staring down at her adorably pursed lips, he felt an insistent warmth invading his heart, overflowing and spilling past its fretted barriers. God in heaven, he was tired of fighting his desire for her. It was exhausting to struggle against something so overwhelming. Like trying not to breathe.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>I absolutely LOVED this one. Delightfully entertaining, and at times hilariously funny. This was an enemies to lovers connection that was incredibly addicting. There were several scenes that I wanted to read over and over again. Romance writing at its best. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“There is nothing on earth more beautiful to me than your smile…no sound sweeter than your laughter…no pleasure greater than holding you in my arms. I realized today that I could never live without you, stubborn little hellion that you are. In this life and the next, you’re my only hope of happiness."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>There were a few things that I thought were a bit over the top. Mostly regarding that bizarre ending. But I still couldn't say that they took anything away from the story. Was it realistic? NO! But honestly isn't that why we read these books in the first place? And now, I'm dying to see how she redeems our hero of book 3. An impossible feat? We shall see. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8120593139009592298" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_102174842" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/102174842" />
    <a title="Lover of Romance" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3709091-lover-of-romance"><img alt="Lover of Romance" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458253423p2/3709091.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/102174842?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lover of Romance" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lover of Romance" href="/user/show/3709091-lover-of-romance">Lover of Romance</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3709091-lover-of-romance?shelf=favorites-shelf">favorites-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3709091-lover-of-romance?shelf=genre-historical-romance">genre-historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3709091-lover-of-romance?shelf=regency">regency</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3709091-lover-of-romance?shelf=victorian">victorian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer102174842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8802486322412350488">This review was originally posted on<a href='http://addictedtoromance.org/2017/11/25/book-review-it-happened-one-autumn-by-lisa-kleypas/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'> Addicted To Romance</a><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1511665967i/24534719._SX540_.png' alt='' width='600' height='100' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><strong>It Happened One Autumn </strong>is a story that I have loved and adored ever since it was published. This book is the second book in the  Wallflower series and one of the best historical series that has ever been written. Now I will say that there is much to love about this book, <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1511665967i/24534720.jpg' alt='' width='304' height='494' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>and even though I don't love it quite as much as Devil in Winter or Scandal in Spring, there is so much to adore about this book.<br/><br/>The Key Players of<strong> It Happened One Autumn </strong>a</span>
  <span id="freeText8802486322412350488" style="display:none">This review was originally posted on<a href="http://addictedtoromance.org/2017/11/25/book-review-it-happened-one-autumn-by-lisa-kleypas/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"> Addicted To Romance</a><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1511665967i/24534719._SX540_.png" alt="" width="600" height="100" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><strong>It Happened One Autumn </strong>is a story that I have loved and adored ever since it was published. This book is the second book in the  Wallflower series and one of the best historical series that has ever been written. Now I will say that there is much to love about this book, <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1511665967i/24534720.jpg" alt="" width="304" height="494" class="gr-hostedUserImg">and even though I don't love it quite as much as Devil in Winter or Scandal in Spring, there is so much to adore about this book.<br><br>The Key Players of<strong> It Happened One Autumn </strong>are:<br> <br> 	 Marcus, Lord Westcliff, London's most eligible Aristocrat, full of responsibilities, domineering at times and in control. <br> 	 Lillian, An American miss who is looking to marry a title....feisty, rebellious, and unconventional. <br> <br>The story begins when Lillian and her sister come to a house party being hosted by the Westcliff's in their country manor home. She and her sister Daisy, are both spirited and always tend to get into trouble. Lillian has no plans on even trying to pursue Westcliff because she has no desire to marry someone so stuffy and pompous and its obvious that Marcus has no interest in Lillian but they do like to argue with each other. :) Marcus protests very strongly upon the arrival of Lillian and her sister coming and its apparent that there is some strong attraction between Marcus and Lillian but they don't want to admit it to themselves. So we seem them just play around with each other at first, not admitting the attraction they have toward each other and then they share a kiss and all reservations go out the window because its way more explosive than they at first want to admit even to themselves. The phrase "she/he doth protest too much" definitely comes into play. They definitely start acting on their physical attraction to each other, but there are other factors involved that seem to cause a conflict on whether they will act on how they are feeling. Marcus especially knows that he wants a biddable wife and Lillian is way too contrary for his liking. But when his friend St.Vincent starts trying his hand at courting Lillian....all of Marcus' reserve go out the window.<br><br>What is most fun about this book is the interaction between Marcus and Lillian. They definitely have sparks going on and its so entertaining to see them banter and try to battle with their words. Even though they are very different from each other, they are also both very stubborn, strong personalities and domineering. They are way more alike than they are different as far as their personalities are concerned and its probably why they fight their attraction so much at first. But soon emotion starts to enter into their relationship and adds a bit more unique dynamic. But what is the most important element is those tender sweet moments that develop between the two that is at odds with their spirited moments together. I love how poignant this story felt so many times and it comes upon the reader unexpectedly.<br> 
  <strong>
    
      “Rest. You’ll need to regain your strength...because once we’re married, I won’t be able to leave you alone. I’ll want to love you every hour, every minute of the day.” He nestled her more closely against him. “There is nothing on earth more beautiful to me than your smile...no sound sweeter than your laughter...no pleasure greater than holding you in my arms. I realized today that I could never live without you, stubborn little hellion that you are. In this life and the next, you’re my only hope of happiness. Tell me, Lillian, dearest love...how can you have reached so far inside my heart?” He paused to kiss her damp silken skin...and smiled as the wisp of a feminine snore broke the peaceful silence.
    
  </strong>
 <br>Another fun aspect to the story that is prevalent through the whole series is the friendship between the four women or the "wallflowers" and I love seeing how they help each other find husbands even if it doesn't happen the way they plan on. There is so much warmth and affection these women have for each other and will do anything for each other and I adore that. Here below is two of my favorite scenes that I just had to share.<br> 
  <strong>“Annabelle, what happened to you?” Lillian asked the next morning. “You look dreadful. Why aren’t you wearing your riding habit? I thought you were going to try out the jumping course this morning. And why did you disappear</strong>
  <br>
  <strong>so suddenly last night? It’s not like you to simply vanish without saying—”</strong>
 <br> 
  <strong>“I didn’t have a choice in the matter,” Annabelle said testily, folding her fingers around the delicate bowl of a porcelain teacup. Looking pale and exhausted, her blue eyes ringed with dark shadows, she swallowed a mouthful of heavily sweetened tea before continuing. “It was that blasted perfume of yours—as soon as he caught one whiff of it, he went berserk.”</strong>
 <br> 
  <strong>Shocked, Lillian tried to take in the information, her stomach plummeting. “It… it had an effect on Westcliff, then?” she managed to ask.</strong>
 <br> <strong>“Good Lord, not Lord Westcliff.” Annabelle rubbed her weary eyes. “He couldn’t have cared less what I smelled like. It was my husband who went completely mad. After he caught the scent of that stuff, he dragged me up to our room and…well, suffice it to say, Mr. Hunt kept me awake all night. All night</strong> ,<strong>” she repeated in sullen emphasis</strong>,<strong> and drank deeply of the tea.</strong> <br> 
  <strong>“Doing what?” Daisy asked blankly.</strong>
 <br> 
  <strong>Lillian, who was feeling a rush of relief that Lord Westcliff had not been attracted to Annabelle while she</strong>
  <br>
  <strong>was wearing the perfume, gave her younger sister a derisive glance. “What do you think they were doing? Playing a few hands of Find-the-Lady?”</strong>
 <br><br> 
  <strong>
    
      “Wait a minute,” Daisy said suspiciously, coming to Lillian’s side.<br>“We’ve met Evie’s cousin Eustace before. Lillian, do you remember the ball at Winterbourne House?” Her eyes narrowed accusingly. “He was the one who broke the chair, wasn’t he, Evie?”<br>Evie confirmed Daisy’s question with an inarticulate murmur.<br>“Good God!” Lillian exclaimed, “you are not considering marrying him, Evie!”<br>Annabelle wore a puzzled expression. “How did he break the chair? Does he have a foul temper? Did he throw it?”<br>“He broke it by sitting on it,” Lillian said with a scowl.<br>“Cousin Eustace is rather l-large boned,” Evie admitted.<br>“Cousin Eustace has more chins than I’ve got fingers,” Lillian said impatiently. “And he was so busy filling his face during the ball that he couldn’t be bothered to make conversation.”<br>“When I went to shake his hand,” Daisy added, “I came away with a half-eaten wing of roast chicken.”<br>“He forgot that he was holding it,” Evie said apologetically. “He did say he was sorry for ruining your glove, as I recall.”<br>Daisy frowned. “That didn’t bother me nearly as much as the question of where he was hiding the rest of the chicken.”
    
  </strong>
 <br><strong>It Happened One Autumn </strong>is a laugh out loud romance that will give you tingles and happy feels, it's a story that is packed with lively banter, boisterous characters, tender romantic moments and characters that you will fall head over heels in love with!!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1511665967i/24534721.png" alt="" width="500" height="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1511665967i/24534723._SX540_.png" alt="" width="600" height="100" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>[foogallery id="19066"]<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1511665967i/24534722._SX540_.png" alt="" width="600" height="100" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="http://addictedtoromance.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1499527757i/23242699.jpg" alt=" photo Addicted To Romance Reviews 2_zpsplp8m0tb.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
