<div id="review_1185584628" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1185584628" />
    <a title="Vicky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21619434-vicky"><img alt="Vicky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461163761p2/21619434.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1185584628?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vicky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vicky" href="/user/show/21619434-vicky">Vicky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21619434-vicky?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21619434-vicky?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21619434-vicky?shelf=2015-reads">2015-reads</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1185584628" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13670571660692359852"><b>DNF at 67%.</b> (I was so thoroughly repulsed by something that happened at this point that I couldn’t bring myself to continue.)<br/><br/>It seems I’m going to be <i>that person</i>. There are many high ratings/glowing reviews for <i>It happened One Autumn</i> and I really wanted mine to be among them, but unfortunately it wasn’t meant to be. The thing is, <b>I totally get why so many of my GR friends liked this book. The bold, strong-willed, potty-mouthed heroine won me over from the start. The relationship of the main coup</b></span>
  <span id="freeText13670571660692359852" style="display:none"><b>DNF at 67%.</b> (I was so thoroughly repulsed by something that happened at this point that I couldn’t bring myself to continue.)<br><br>It seems I’m going to be <i>that person</i>. There are many high ratings/glowing reviews for <i>It happened One Autumn</i> and I really wanted mine to be among them, but unfortunately it wasn’t meant to be. The thing is, <b>I totally get why so many of my GR friends liked this book. The bold, strong-willed, potty-mouthed heroine won me over from the start. The relationship of the main couple was great with the banter, bickering and constant sexual tension that led to an explosive, <i>yespleasemore</i> chemistry. UNTIL this happened---&gt;</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b>The hero took advantage of the heroine and had sex with her while she was drunk.</b> I know what some of you might say: <i>She actually wanted him, so he wasn’t taking advantage of her.</i> <b>YES, HE WAS.</b> Wanting something is not the same as to be willing to do it. Many people wish to do certain things but would never actually do them because they are aware that those actions have consequences they are not prepared to deal with. Yes, the heroine was attracted to the hero, but she was aware that having sex with him would “ruin” her for any other men who might have asked for her hand in marriage <i>and she was determined to marry</i>. Would she have voluntarily given in to their passion and thrown to hell her chances at marriage? We will never know, because the hero took away her choice when he decided her sexual debut should be at that moment when she couldn’t give her consent. <br>The next thing some people might argue is: <i>She was conscious enough to recognize him and she went along with the things he did so that means she gave her consent.</i> <b>NO, IT DOESN’T.</b> We are not talking about someone who had a little bit to drink and still retained all her faculties. She drunk (as the hero well knew) half a bottle of brandy, she was slurring her words, she needed to be picked up in his arms to climb the stairs because she was too unsteady on her feet to walk by herself and she was so out of her mind that at one point she wondered ALOUD whether she was dreaming. The hero acknowledged (and I quote him): <b>"She was foxed, staggering, tap-hackled, top-heavy, shot-in-the-neck, staggering drunk."</b> Him having sex with her while she was in that condition wasn’t sexy for me. It was disgusting. It was rape. And I’m never going to be ok with that.<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422844429i/13553565._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Damn it, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/27847.Lisa_Kleypas" title="Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Lisa Kleypas</a>!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422679418ra/13534074.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There had been previous, though smaller, instances that showed that streak of the hero's character <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[At one point he embraced and kissed her while she explicitly and repeatedly told him to get off her.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422844582i/13553610._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, so I guess I shouldn’t have been so surprised when the big "no no" scene happened, but I was. And I was most definitely not ok with any of it. <br><br><b>I want to cry from anger and disappointment. This could have easily been a 4 star read for me. There were many amazing things in this book: at times I lmao, I smiled liked crazy and I relished the delicious sexual tension. BUT there are certain topics I feel very strongly about and I can’t gloss over them. I just can’t.</b> Why, Lisa Kleypas? Why did you have to ruin it all by introducing a completely unnecessary and repulsive element?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381112457ra/4242982.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1929623740" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1929623740" />
    <a title="Mo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11856352-mo"><img alt="Mo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1371247812p2/11856352.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1929623740?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mo" href="/user/show/11856352-mo">Mo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6561363-it-happened-one-autumn">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1929623740" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8871175782579971406">Another good read. Love to see the aristocracy brought to their knees by the lower classes! And by an American, no less.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1488902710i/22166713.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Marcus, Lord Westcliff is one of the most eligible bachelors in England. He knows it is his duty to marry well. Someone of his own station ... but he is attracted to a brash American girl. And he is not happy. He does not like her, he does not want to be attracted to her! And the feeling is mutual from her.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>And once he had passed judgment on someone, he rarely changed his opi</b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText8871175782579971406" style="display:none">Another good read. Love to see the aristocracy brought to their knees by the lower classes! And by an American, no less.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1488902710i/22166713.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Marcus, Lord Westcliff is one of the most eligible bachelors in England. He knows it is his duty to marry well. Someone of his own station ... but he is attracted to a brash American girl. And he is not happy. He does not like her, he does not want to be attracted to her! And the feeling is mutual from her.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>And once he had passed judgment on someone, he rarely changed his opinion.</b>

<span id="freeTextContainer15765480093853053675">Meet <b>Lillian</b> rich lady from America whose parents ship her off to England to find herself a man <i>#thanks-a-fucking-lot-Dad</i><br/> <br/>The only problem is that these stuffy english men want a lady of modesty and Lillian? <b>Lillian don't do none of that shit</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493752793ra/22649730.gif' width='200' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>

  <span id="freeText15765480093853053675" style="display:none">Meet <b>Lillian</b> rich lady from America whose parents ship her off to England to find herself a man <i>#thanks-a-fucking-lot-Dad</i><br> <br>The only problem is that these stuffy english men want a lady of modesty and Lillian? <b>Lillian don't do none of that shit</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493752793ra/22649730.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>“The good news is that your husband seems to be on the way.”<br>“If so, the bastard is late,” Lillian retorted, causing Daisy and Evie to laugh.”</i>
</b><br><br>Her family is invited to stay at Lord Westcliff’s home as it is the height of the season and bachelors are everywhere....except Lillian can’t seem to escape the one man she hates: <b>Marcus Marsden</b><br><br><b>
  <i>“He’s just a man, dear. I’m sure he orders his servants to help him put his trousers on one leg at a time, like everyone else.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476729981ra/20874680.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved her brash, foul-mouthed, outspoken American ways. <b>I wanted her to bring Westcliff to his knees.</b> This story was so entertaining from how they bicker, fight, challenge, argue, hate, steal kisses, and lust after each other. <br><br><b>
  <i>“There is something about you that makes me feel terribly wicked. You make me want to do shocking things. Maybe it's because you're so proper. Your necktie is never crooked, and your shoes are always shiny. Sometimes when I look at you, I want to tear off all your buttons. Or set your trousers on fire.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464644478ra/19259738.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh how they fought! Their arguing and sniping resulted in a pile of sexual tension and Lillian the troublemaker got them in ridicious hilarious situations:<br><br><b>
  <i>“Would you mind telling me why you were drinking pear brandy in the middle of the afternoon?”<br>“Because I couldn’ open the sherry.”<br>His lips twitched. “What I meant was, why were you drinking at all?”</i>
</b><br>Same girlll sameeeee<br><br>She is so sassy and such a spitfire. I love how Westcliff was hesitant towards her <b>but he knew that he needed his equal</b> Someone to challenge him, make him laugh, make him angry....and that someone is Cece! I mean Lillian right the protagonist <br><br><b>
  <i>“Fear you?” she said without thinking. “Good God, I would never do that.”<br>Easing her head back, Westcliff looked at her while a slow smile spread across his face. “No, you wouldn’t,” he agreed. “You’d spit in the devil’s eye if it suited you.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1523566605ra/25367827.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And the romance? Oh sweetie my heart was just a puddle, reading Westcliff come to terms with his feelings:<br><br><b>
  <i>“Run barefoot on the front lawn. Eat pudding with your fingers. Tell me to go to hell as often as you like. I want you just as you are”</i>
</b><br>Goddamn it my heart, Westcliff is just da man<br><br><b>
  <i>“My lord,” came Daisy’s anxious voice, delaying him briefly. “You will find her, won’t you?”<br>“Yes,” he said without hesitation. “And then I’m going to strangle her.”</i>
</b><br>I love how he is both worrying about her...and threatening her at the same time like boyyyyyy <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1523566605ra/25367828.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Overall, this was a great read and definitely my favorite out of the series <b>becauses I loved Lillian’s character</b> and felt she was more relatable than the others. Plus Westcliff was so done with her shit but couldn’t seem to stop himself from joining the trouble. Great read, 4 stars</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer96179990&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer96179990" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16807218404976579884"><i>It all started with a kiss...</i><br/><br/>There was never any <s>love</s> friendliness between Marcus, Lord Westcliff, and Lillian Bowman, but when Lillian and her family come to stay at Westcliff's for the month long house party, a desperate kiss in the garden brings a passion for each other to the forefront. During the extent of her stay there, Lillian and Westcliff battle their attraction while also starting to get to know each other and, dare I say it? Like each other! Sure, they still have their quarrels, but </span>
  <span id="freeText16807218404976579884" style="display:none"><i>It all started with a kiss...</i><br /><br />There was never any <s>love</s> friendliness between Marcus, Lord Westcliff, and Lillian Bowman, but when Lillian and her family come to stay at Westcliff's for the month long house party, a desperate kiss in the garden brings a passion for each other to the forefront. During the extent of her stay there, Lillian and Westcliff battle their attraction while also starting to get to know each other and, dare I say it? Like each other! Sure, they still have their quarrels, but they also manage to have some fun together, and miraculously, they feel <i>comfortable</i> together.<br /><br />One day when Lillian manages to get herself drunk, she and Westcliff finally give into their passion for each other. When Westcliff demands that they get married, Lillian naturally rejects him and is furious the next morning when she finds that he talked to her father. After confronting Westcliff about it, and an awkward encounter with Sebastian, Lord St. Vincent, her other potential suitor, Lillian finds that Westcliff really does care for her, he just went about expressing it in the wrong way. Later that night, Lillian goes to Westcliff and she finally agrees to marry him.<br /><br />The next morning, Westcliff's mother demands an audience with Lillian, outside in the farthest part of the garden. During which time they have a nasty confrontation and the countess lets someone kidnap Lillian. She wakes later to find herself resting against Lord St. Vincent, who is taking her to Gretna Green to force her to marry him, for she's an heiress and he is in need of money. Upon threatening his mother's life, Westcliff finds out that St. Vincent kidnapped Lillian and races out to find them.<br /><br />Lillian manages to escape St. Vincent when she is left alone in a room while he is out checking their new team of horses. To her surprise and delight, Westcliff is there and they are reunited. Until St. Vincent walks into the room, not knowing what awaits him, and Westcliff beats him to a pulp. In the end, St. Vincent is sent back to his house and the next day Westcliff and Lillian set off for Gretna Green to get married.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />What to say about this book other than it's utterly and completely amazing...Hmmm...I loved the Wallflowers and seeing their dynamic. Lillian and Daisy were hilarious together, and I really look forward to reading Scandal in Spring. Marcus, Lord Westcliff, is now the love of my life and I can't wait to see him in the other Wallflowers books. Now on to further reflection on the book...<br /><br />Lord Westcliff is probably one of my favorite male characters now, not just among Lisa Kleypas' heroes but in general. He is strong, powerful, and takes his responsibilities seriously. He's stubborn, loyal, arrogant, and guarded. I loved seeing him go from arrogant and "hating" Lillian to realizing just how much he cares for her and accepting that he needs her in his life.<br /><br />I adored Lillian and how stubborn she was in every instance, but I also enjoyed seeing her transform like Westcliff. I loved, too, when she realized that she was exactly what Westcliff needed and that she loved him. Her interactions with her sister, Daisy, were great and I liked seeing her interact with Annabelle and Evie, too.<br /><br />I myself felt betrayed when Sebastian, Lord St. Vincent, kidnapped Lillian. While I'd figured it out beforehand, I still got really upset when it was revealed that it was him and with all the threats that he made, namely the prospect of raping her. So, I felt vindicated when Westcliff beat his butt! Now, don't get me wrong, I still like St. Vincent, but that was a very rocky time in our relationship. And I look forward to seeing him brought to his knees in Devil in Winter.<br /><br />I'm very glad to have read this book, and discovered my love of Lord Westcliff!, and I look forward to reading the rest of the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16807218404976579884" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17587095475613903117"><b> 3.75 Stars</b><br/><br/><b>Overall Opinion: </b>I was totally loving this book the first two thirds! I was so happy with the hate-to-love type relationship they had and I was just anxiously waiting for them to come to their senses and be a couple! I'm SO incredibly disappointed in the ending though. I wanted some time with them as a couple! We get so much of the h hemming and hawing about the idea of them together and how they would potentially fight all the time, and we don't actually see them as a couple! Even if</span>
  <span id="freeText17587095475613903117" style="display:none"><b> 3.75 Stars</b><br /><br /><b>Overall Opinion: </b>I was totally loving this book the first two thirds! I was so happy with the hate-to-love type relationship they had and I was just anxiously waiting for them to come to their senses and be a couple! I'm SO incredibly disappointed in the ending though. I wanted some time with them as a couple! We get so much of the h hemming and hawing about the idea of them together and how they would potentially fight all the time, and we don't actually see them as a couple! Even if it was a fight I think it would've been better than what we got tbh. I don't think I can justify a higher rating with an ending like that 😕<br /><br /><b>Brief Summary of the Storyline: </b> This is Lillian and Marcus's story. They are acquaintances through Lillian's father being a potential business partner with Marcus. Marcus is considered the most eligible bachelor in England, and Lillian is an American that is in search for a noble husband. They butt heads but also have a strong underlying attraction to one another. The more time they spend together, the more they find it hard to see the good things about one another and fall in love. There are some funny moments, some good banter, a few sexy times, and some family drama...and they get a HEA ending.<br /><br /><b>POV:</b> This alternated between focusing on Lillian and Marcus in 3rd person narrative.<br /><br /><b>Overall Pace of Story: </b> Good until the ending (see closure section below). I never skimmed and I thought it flowed well otherwise.<br /><br /><b>Instalove:</b> No, they take a while to develop stronger feelings. It was actually a hate-to-love type relationship.<br /><br /><b>H rating:</b> 4 stars. Marcus. I liked him. He was broody, but also really caring and sweet when needed. <br /><br /><b>h rating:</b> 4 stars. Lillian. I liked her. She was improper, and she never apologized for it! She was a little overly stubborn at times, but I took that to be just her character.<br /><br /><b>Sadness level: </b>Low, no tissues needed<br /><br /><b>Push/Pull:</b> Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[They both push away at times, and they both also pursue the relationship at times.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Heat level:</b> Hot. They have some hot tension, chemistry, and scenes -- but not so much it takes away from the story.<br /><br /><b>Descriptive sex:</b> Yes<br /><br /><b>OW/OM drama:</b> Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[One of the H's friends pursues the h because he is in financial trouble and needs her fortune. This causes some drama for the couple.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Sex scene with OW or OM:</b> No<br /><br /><b>Cheating: </b> No<br /><br /><b>Separation:</b> Not in the relationship sense <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[They are separated physically shortly, but there was no mention or suggestion of other partners during this time.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Possible Triggers: </b>Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Child abuse (H - off page through mentions), virgin h, and kidnapping/violence (on page).  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Closure: </b> This had a really abrupt ending with not nearly enough closure for me!! I wanted to have a glimpse into their future! I wanted to experience them actually together -- not just sexually but in love. The epilogue was used entirely for setting up the next book (which I hate). I would still reluctantly call this a HEA, but I am not at all satisfied with the ending <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[they are married <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br /><b>How I got it:</b> I got it on loan through my public library and Amazon.<br /><br /><b>Safety:</b> This one should be <u>Safe</u> for most safety gang readers<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />- <b>Does Not</b> have cheating<br />- <b>Does Not</b> have a descriptive sex scene with OW/OM<br />- <b> Does</b> have both the h and H pushing away<br />- <b> Does Not</b> have a separation between the h and H<br />- <b> Does Not</b> have abuse by mcs<br />- <b> Does Not</b> have OTT sad parts<br />- <b>Does </b> have a HEA ending (see above) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_155092755" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/155092755" />
    <a title="Ronyell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell"><img alt="Ronyell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506581787p2/1169488.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/155092755?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ronyell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ronyell" href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell">Ronyell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=british-hero-or-heroine">british-hero-or-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=manners">manners</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=ronyell-s-epinions-reviews">ronyell-s-epinions-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=adult-book">adult-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=english-books">english-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=lisa-kleypas">lisa-kleypas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=my-blog-reviews">my-blog-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=aar-top-100-romance-books-2010">aar-top-100-romance-books-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer155092755" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17526123870916981608">After reading Lisa Kleypas’ previous books <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/674220.Again_the_Magic__Wallflowers___0_5_' title='Again the Magic (Wallflowers, #0.5) by Lisa Kleypas' rel='nofollow noopener'>Again The Magic</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/114162.Secrets_of_a_Summer_Night__Wallflowers___1_' title='Secrets of a Summer Night (Wallflowers, #1) by Lisa Kleypas' rel='nofollow noopener'>Secrets of a Summer Night</a>, I just had to read the second book in the Wallflower series called “It Happened One Autumn” which stars Lillian Bowman and Marcus, Lord Westcliff! “It Happened One Autumn” is so full of drama, romance one awesome hero and heroine team that any romance fan will eat this book up!<br/><br/>American heiress Lillian Bowman came to London along with her family to pursue a worthy husband of her status. However, Lillian seem</span>
  <span id="freeText17526123870916981608" style="display:none">After reading Lisa Kleypas’ previous books <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/674220.Again_the_Magic__Wallflowers___0_5_" title="Again the Magic (Wallflowers, #0.5) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Again The Magic</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/114162.Secrets_of_a_Summer_Night__Wallflowers___1_" title="Secrets of a Summer Night (Wallflowers, #1) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Secrets of a Summer Night</a>, I just had to read the second book in the Wallflower series called “It Happened One Autumn” which stars Lillian Bowman and Marcus, Lord Westcliff! “It Happened One Autumn” is so full of drama, romance one awesome hero and heroine team that any romance fan will eat this book up!<br /><br />American heiress Lillian Bowman came to London along with her family to pursue a worthy husband of her status. However, Lillian seems to loathe the handsome yet headstrong Earl of Stony Cross Park, Marcus, Lord Westcliff as she believes that he is a snob and Marcus seems to loathe Lillian also since she is so stubborn. But this couple will soon realize that their differences might bring them closer together.<br /><br />*My, I am so breathless!* Oh my goodness, this book clearly defines what a true romance novel is all about! I just practically love everything about this book – the characters, the plot and the romance! I loved the way that Lisa Kleypas made the book extremely dramatic yet hilarious at the same time and what I really loved about Lisa Kleypas’ writing is how she made Lillian Bowman and Marcus, Lord Westcliff’s relationship seem so hilarious, especially when they are arguing so much. I usually disapprove of couples fighting in romance novels, but in this case, the way that Marcus and Lillian argued was so cute! It is like one moment Lillian and Marcus are arguing about how they should ruled each other’s lives and then the next minute, they are making love to each other! <br /><br />As much as I loved the plot, the characters were the true highlights of this story! My favorite characters in this book are of course, Lillian Bowman and Marcus, Lord Westcliff! Lillian Bowman is truly one heroine I truly enjoyed as she Is not afraid to speak her mind, even in the face of danger and I loved the way that she easily stands up to Marcus and speaks on her opinions, which is an aspect of her character that I truly loved. I also loved Lillian’s close relationship with the other Wallflowers which included her sister Daisy Bowman, Annabelle Peyton and Evangeline Jenner. Now, I would like to talk about Marcus, Lord Westcliff and man is he something else! Marcus, Lord Westcliff is one amazing hero as he is described as being muscular yet lean and he is truly headstrong and also speaks his mind! What I really loved about Marcus is how he truly has a heart full of gold, especially when it concerns Lillian and when Lillian is in grave danger, oh boy, watch out because Marcus can be really frightening when he is angry, which I really admit made me more attracted to his character! I could go on and on about Marcus, but that would be an extremely long list to go through! This romance novel is sex scenes galore as it is full of lovemaking scenes between Marcus and Lillian that will have your hairs stand on your ends!<br /><br />There are many sex scenes throughout this book, so anyone who is uncomfortable with reading sex scenes might want to skip over these scenes when reading this book.<br /><br />All in all, “It Happened One Autumn” is clearly a novel that defines what a true romance novel is all about and also features my favorite hero, Marcus, Lord Westcliff! I am definitely going out of my way to read the next book in the Wallflower series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/114166.Devil_in_Winter__Wallflowers___3_" title="Devil in Winter (Wallflowers, #3) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Devil in Winter</a>!<br /><br /><b>Review is also on: <a href="http://rabbitearsbookblog.blogspot.com/2012/04/it-happened-one-autumn-by-lisa-kleypas.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabbit Ears Book Blog</a></b><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17526123870916981608" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3575839-suzanne-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=enemies-to-lovers">enemies-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3575839-suzanne-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=hero-hot-male-in-my-harem">hero-hot-male-in-my-harem</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3575839-suzanne-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=heroines-i-love">heroines-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3575839-suzanne-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=hero-arrogant-but-i-love-him">hero-arrogant-but-i-love-him</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3575839-suzanne-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=genre-historical-romance">genre-historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3575839-suzanne-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=author-lisa-kleypas">author-lisa-kleypas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3575839-suzanne-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=hero-alpha">hero-alpha</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98335924" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1397959254581398404"><a href='http://www.underthecoversbookblog.com/2012/02/review-it-happened-one-autumn-by-lisa-kleypas.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380333934i/693541.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Miss Annabelle Payton, Miss Lillian Bowman, Miss Evangeline Jenner and Miss Daisy Bowman are regular sights at the peripheral of a ballroom. Each young lady has their own difficulties making them untenable prospects to the bachelors of the ton. However, they strike up an unlikely friendship each vowing to help the others out to find a husband by means fair and foul. After Annabelle’s successful marriage to Mr Hunt, it is now the turn of the dollar princess, Miss Lillian Bowman, she is both i</span>
  <span id="freeText1397959254581398404" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.underthecoversbookblog.com/2012/02/review-it-happened-one-autumn-by-lisa-kleypas.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380333934i/693541.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Miss Annabelle Payton, Miss Lillian Bowman, Miss Evangeline Jenner and Miss Daisy Bowman are regular sights at the peripheral of a ballroom. Each young lady has their own difficulties making them untenable prospects to the bachelors of the ton. However, they strike up an unlikely friendship each vowing to help the others out to find a husband by means fair and foul. After Annabelle’s successful marriage to Mr Hunt, it is now the turn of the dollar princess, Miss Lillian Bowman, she is both irreverent and bold, and she views the lords of the realm as insufferable bores, most especially the stuffy Lord Westcliff...<br><br>Another fine addition to the Wallflower quartet, the story of Miss Lillian Bowman and Marcus, Lord Westcliff is a lively, funny and romantic story. I loved both the characters, and although at first they seem like complete opposites, with Westcliff giving a very austere impression and Lillian being very outgoing, I thought that under the surface they had similar characteristics, both domineering, stubborn, convinced they are always right, prideful, and had the tendency to hide their feelings behind various facades. But that seems to give them a rather negative character assessment, but that is far from the truth, they are also both fiercely loyal with lively and caring personalities. <br><br>The romance between the two was inevitable, and was started really in “Secrets of a Summer Night,” as demonstrated by the rounder-in-knickers incident *giggles in remembrance* They are both drawn to each other despite the rather low opinions they have of one another at the beginning. Westcliff thinks that Lillian is an abrasive, ill mannered, savage; however, I wonder how much of his rather unreasonable hostility was a defence mechanism, and Lillian thought he was an autocratic boring brute, although it seems that is more a reaction to his behaviour. I like how as they both get to know each other, they begin to realize they are more then they appear and perhaps they are exactly what the other needs, despite of and maybe because of their flaws. <br><br>As well as romantic relationships, you also see the group of friends, the wallflowers, come together again, I love seeing their friendship blossom and continue, and the cast of different characters in this series is, apart from the romances, one of the best things about it. You get to see the continuation of Annabelle and Simon’s HEA and the further character development of both Evie and Daisy in preparation for their own books.<br><br>There was also in the introduction of the infamous rake Lord St. Vincent, one of LK’s most famous heroes. He is a rather notorious scoundrel and rake, and despite his physical charms and his “animal magnetism” a very cold and immoral person. He plays the part of villain in this book, but is there anything but self interest and hatred below pretty facade, hmmm, I guess I will have to read on to find out...<br><br>Again in this book, the writing was witty and funny in both the dialogue and storytelling, it keeps you engaged, effortlessly giving you a window into the Wallflowers world. I would recommend this to all Lisa Kleypas fans, and those who love historical romance. It is well written, with well fleshed out characters that feel like old friends and a believable love story.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456264496i/18212231._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="1397959254581398404" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1285720190" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1285720190" />
    <a title="Daniella" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43278962-daniella"><img alt="Daniella" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456404814p2/43278962.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1285720190?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniella" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniella" href="/user/show/43278962-daniella">Daniella</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1285720190" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17746473543599766688"><b>Solid 4 stars.</b> <br/><br/>I've never been a chronological reader; I just pick up whatever book that catches my fancy. When I read <i>It Happened One Autumn</i> for the first time, I had no idea what I was getting into—I started the series with it. The description had simply intrigued me, since I've always been a fan of the "stoic-hero-cracks-under-the-heroine's-spell" trope, a la Mr. Darcy and Elizabeth Bennet. <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450172755ra/17389483.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>But this time around, after re-reading the series, <b>I find myself having a totally deeper appreciation </b></span>
  <span id="freeText17746473543599766688" style="display:none"><b>Solid 4 stars.</b> <br><br>I've never been a chronological reader; I just pick up whatever book that catches my fancy. When I read <i>It Happened One Autumn</i> for the first time, I had no idea what I was getting into—I started the series with it. The description had simply intrigued me, since I've always been a fan of the "stoic-hero-cracks-under-the-heroine's-spell" trope, a la Mr. Darcy and Elizabeth Bennet. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450172755ra/17389483.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>But this time around, after re-reading the series, <b>I find myself having a totally deeper appreciation of the book</b>, primarily because I saw how Marcus' character developed since the prequel. In <i>Again the Magic</i>, he was the protective brother whose patience and understanding knew no boundaries. In <i>Secrets of a Summer Night</i>, he was the loyal friend who would risk his neck to save those he cared about. <br><br>And in this book? <b>He was the perfect Mr. Darcy—albeit the more wanton and less self-controlled version</b>. Terribly frustrating, slightly conceited, and logical to a fault, he thought he had his life all planned out: fulfil his duties as Lord Westcliff, find an amiable wife, beget sons, and that's it. Well, that is,<b> until he met the one woman who turned his carefully laid plans on its heels—Lillian Bowman</b>.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429742919ra/14626145.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I remember hating Lillian, but I'm glad to see that she wasn't nearly as irritating as I thought. Yes, she was far from being a stellar character. Yes, she had her TSTL moments. And yes, she was frustrating and illogical with her refusal to marry Marcus despite of being thoroughly shagged by him. But that's judging her in isolation.<br><br> <b>If you pair her up with Marcus, you'd see that she's simply perfect for him</b>. She brought him back to Earth with her well-deserved set-downs. She provoked him like no other woman did, and made him <i>feel</i> things. She made him get off his self-created pedestal and see himself for the mortal that he was.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450172755ra/17389484.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>In short, she was everything he needed.</b> And I think Lisa Kleypas captured that nicely in Marcus' proposal:<br><blockquote>“If you won’t marry me for the sake of your own honor, then do it for the sake of everyone who would have to tolerate me otherwise. <b>Marry me because I need someone who will help me to laugh at myself. Because someone has to teach me how to whistle.</b> Marry me, Lillian…because I have the most irresistible fascination for your ears.”</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450172755ra/17389485.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>While I am thoroughly convinced that Lillian and Marcus belonged to each other, I just couldn't help but feel bad at how Sebastian was treated here. Okay, okay, so he deserved getting his ass whipped. Fine. But I'm an intensely loyal fan of his and Evie's, and I couldn't help but cringe at some parts of this book. Especially when he flirted with Lillian. Ugh. <br><br>Overall, though, <b>I really loved this</b>. Would I re-read it again in the future? Sure. Would I recommend it? Hell, yes.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450172755ra/17389486.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="17746473543599766688" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('g5UmyTzferV1pexhD8YpzRaXrJJwMRRFKmpyL2Zr8t5CxlhaZs2KFJMq0wTvdpDpxKV8aKsS/yROFIt+RDCuPQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('L+bGLOKngaWwI+Vp6FLeXGHEFZx3/wmKEQ+kAAkaPLrutbi/uLVxBFas2gwI4md4s/bFZqzc4ut1cV1RK0FgWQ==')})
  }
